  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_41051411-b392-4db7-bd6e-96859cb979db'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer488493256195375501">Claire and her mother are running out of time, but they don't know it. Not yet. Claire is wrapped up with the difficulties of her bourgeoning adulthood—boys, school, friends, identity; Claire's mother, a single mom, is rushed off her feet both at work and at home. They rarely find themselves in the same room at the same time, and it often seems that the only thing they can</span>
  <span id="freeText488493256195375501" style="display:none">Claire and her mother are running out of time, but they don't know it. Not yet. Claire is wrapped up with the difficulties of her bourgeoning adulthood—boys, school, friends, identity; Claire's mother, a single mom, is rushed off her feet both at work and at home. They rarely find themselves in the same room at the same time, and it often seems that the only thing they can count on are notes to each other on the refrigerator door. When home is threatened by a crisis, their relationship experiences a momentous change. Forced to reevaluate the delicate balance between their personal lives and their bond as mother and daughter, Claire and her mother find new love and devotion for one another deeper than anything they had ever imagined.<br /><br />Heartfelt, touching, and unforgettable, <em>Life on the Refrigerator Door</em> is a glimpse into the lives of mothers and daughters everywhere. In this deeply touching novel told through a series of notes written from a loving mother and her devoted fifteen-year-old daughter, debut author Alice Kuipers deftly captures the impenetrable fabric that connects mothers and daughters throughout the world. Moving and rich with emotion, <em>Life on the Refrigerator Door</em> delivers universal lessons about love in a wonderfully simple and poignant narrative.</span>
  <a data-text-id="488493256195375501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_18107052" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18107052" />
    <a title="Kristin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/402298-kristin"><img alt="Kristin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1190642939p2/402298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18107052?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin" href="/user/show/402298-kristin">Kristin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18107052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14337091130242179569">I took a week or so to write my review of this book because I'm still not certain how I truly feel. I admit to having borrowed it from the library's "We recommend" section; I felt it would be a quick 'read whilst waiting on the car line' book. Little did I know forty-five minutes worth of reading would cause such inner strife! <br/><br/>Initially I felt the plot to be terribly contrived in terms of post-it note communication. However, having finished the book I realised several people/families have indeed</span>
  <span id="freeText14337091130242179569" style="display:none">I took a week or so to write my review of this book because I'm still not certain how I truly feel. I admit to having borrowed it from the library's "We recommend" section; I felt it would be a quick 'read whilst waiting on the car line' book. Little did I know forty-five minutes worth of reading would cause such inner strife! <br /><br />Initially I felt the plot to be terribly contrived in terms of post-it note communication. However, having finished the book I realised several people/families have indeed reduced their chats to post-its and text messages. This rather obvious observation depressed me. <br /><br />I found myself angry with both mother and daughter - why were such important conversations being reduced to little 2 by 2 strips of paper? Why couldn't the mother sit down and speak with Claire? I found myself angry with the author. Wasn't she simply perpetuating and/or glorifying this non-approach to face to face, heartfelt verbal exchanges?<br /><br />Yes, I became misty-eyed at the close with the final note on the door - yet it was glaringly too little too late!<br /><br />I suppose this was indeed the author's intent - to point out our lack of communication in this ever increasingly fast-paced, self-centered world. Yet I can't help thinking people may read this and take a different tact - "Oh wasn't that sweet - so touching - so sad!" - texted to a friend while sitting in the local Starbucks!<br /><br />My eleven year old son asked if he could read the book and I said yes - then my 9 year old daughter sat down for a read. The three of us discussed it later (seated at the kitchen table) and all agreed life's conversations are meant to be just that - verbal give and take between individuals.<br /><br />Again, perhaps this discontent was the goal - and perhaps I'm less angry than saddened that people might need to read a book like this to be reminded of what is important in life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14337091130242179569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1843931397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1843931397" />
    <a title="emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58877035-emily"><img alt="emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587215502p2/58877035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1843931397?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emily" href="/user/show/58877035-emily">emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1843931397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5369569028987265688">I read this beautiful little gem of a book, a couple of years ago. You might think to yourself ... Well, alright, cool ... but how can you write a review for a book you barely remember? <br/><br/>I'll tell you how. <br/><br/>You don't write a review, but you write something along the lines of a 'recollection of thoughts'. I might not remember every detail of the book - actually, who am I kidding - I barely remember anything, but a few main themes. <br/><br/>However, I can remember what I felt whilst reading this novel, and y</span>
  <span id="freeText5369569028987265688" style="display:none">I read this beautiful little gem of a book, a couple of years ago. You might think to yourself ... Well, alright, cool ... but how can you write a review for a book you barely remember? <br /><br />I'll tell you how. <br /><br />You don't write a review, but you write something along the lines of a 'recollection of thoughts'. I might not remember every detail of the book - actually, who am I kidding - I barely remember anything, but a few main themes. <br /><br />However, I can remember what I felt whilst reading this novel, and you rarely forget feelings that accompanied you in moments of your life (unless of course, your memory, involuntarily, due to medical reasons, fails you). <br /><br />I remember loving the whole premise of this book. The entire novel is written in note form - a method of communication between a teenage girl and her mother. It was easy to read, quick and intriguing. I believe I read the entire book in a day. <br /><br />It was very, very relatable. I remember there being conversations (in written form, of course) about feeding pet rabbits and buying groceries. <br /><br />It was moving and focused on a very special thing, often overlooked in YA novels, more specifically: the bond between family members. Watching the constantly meandering and uncertain, but always loving relationship between a mother and a daughter was charming to read about. <br /><br />It was heartbreaking, and carried such a deep, meaningful message that every person should hear. The way I interpreted this message was that, we should always make time for the people we love, because we never know when our time will run out. <br /><br />What a great book. <br /><br />If you're looking for a quick read, pick this up, but prepare for a wave of emotions. This book will have your heartstrings in a twist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5369569028987265688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184194474?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Mothers with teenage daughters</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4746016-tiffany?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4746016-tiffany?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4746016-tiffany?shelf=love-stories">love-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4746016-tiffany?shelf=life-issues">life-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4746016-tiffany?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184194474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7750266819599310889"> Okay, I'll admit it...this book had me bawling in the waiting room at the doctor's office yesterday. Everyone thought I was there for bad news. After reading the ending, I could honestly tell the doctor I was doing great. <br/> The title caught my eye first, but when I saw the pages were notes between a mother and daughter, I had to read it. Claire is a teenager struggling to define herself in a life of divorce, friends, boys, and school. Her mom is also struggling as a single mother raising a daugh</span>
  <span id="freeText7750266819599310889" style="display:none"> Okay, I'll admit it...this book had me bawling in the waiting room at the doctor's office yesterday. Everyone thought I was there for bad news. After reading the ending, I could honestly tell the doctor I was doing great. <br /> The title caught my eye first, but when I saw the pages were notes between a mother and daughter, I had to read it. Claire is a teenager struggling to define herself in a life of divorce, friends, boys, and school. Her mom is also struggling as a single mother raising a daughter and working. They rarely see each other. Their lives are recorded by notes on the refrigerator.<br /> The writing is engaging - especially as the word choice and tone change as their lives change. The characters were so believable, I could see them as I read, even though the author never describes their appearance. <br /> The best part of the book was being able to relate to the characters. As a teenager, I found it difficult to communicate with my mom. Now I have a teenage daughter. A few years ago we put a white board on the fridge to remind everyone of important messages, shopping lists, etc. My daughter began to use it as a way to talk to me about things she was feeling or thinking but couldn't say out loud. Her messages made me laugh, and often made me cry, but kept us connected through the dark days of adolescence. Alice Kuiper captures that same connection and love between Claire and her mom. This is a must read book - especially if you have a daughter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7750266819599310889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34762349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5863414699756454621">I'm not sure what to say about this book. I had this listed to-read for quite awhile and finally stumbled upon it yesterday at the Super G. :) <br/>I will admit that I'm glad I didn't pay $15.95 for it. As much as I liked it being that it took me less than 20 minutes to read I would have been a little ticked at that. As it happened I only paid $3.00 for it and for this I am pleased. <br/>The reason I gave this 4 stars instead of 3 is the ending. The ending affected me more than any other part of the book.</span>
  <span id="freeText5863414699756454621" style="display:none">I'm not sure what to say about this book. I had this listed to-read for quite awhile and finally stumbled upon it yesterday at the Super G. :) <br />I will admit that I'm glad I didn't pay $15.95 for it. As much as I liked it being that it took me less than 20 minutes to read I would have been a little ticked at that. As it happened I only paid $3.00 for it and for this I am pleased. <br />The reason I gave this 4 stars instead of 3 is the ending. The ending affected me more than any other part of the book. The book did a good job leading up to the ending but the ending definitely pulled at my heart. Maybe it's because I have a young daughter and it's always been a strong fear of mine that I "miss" time with her. Since she's been born I've always been very conscious of that "missed" time. I don't want to look back one day and realize time was wasted. And this book pinponted that and it also showed how very easy it would be to fall into the trap. <br />I thought it was telling that so many of the notes between Claire and her Mom involved <i>planned</i> meetings. <i>"I'll be back in time to go with you."</i>, <i>"I'm going out for a minute - let's watch a movie tonight."</i> (These are my words - not quotes - the gist of it is the same but I didn't take these word for word.) This type of note showed how easy it is, for anyone, to have great intentions that fall to the wayside. <br />It's a very, very fast book. Any books with one or two sentences on each page would be. But I think Kuiper's did a good job and I'd certainly be willing to read another of her books anytime. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5863414699756454621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12894416453529557901">It is a quick read , about a woman and her daughter who are communicating most of the time through  fridge's notes because they  are rarely  at home at the same time,no wonder the young girl is just a 15 years old spending her entire time between school and hanging out with her friends or babysitting   whilst her mom is a doctor.  They talk almost about everything; relationships, grocery, school, their rabbit peter....and even disease.<br/> The mother suffered from a breast cancer ,unfortunately she </span>
  <span id="freeText12894416453529557901" style="display:none">It is a quick read , about a woman and her daughter who are communicating most of the time through  fridge's notes because they  are rarely  at home at the same time,no wonder the young girl is just a 15 years old spending her entire time between school and hanging out with her friends or babysitting   whilst her mom is a doctor.  They talk almost about everything; relationships, grocery, school, their rabbit peter....and even disease.<br /> The mother suffered from a breast cancer ,unfortunately she could not survive , however the young girl continued writing to her mom in the same way , I even consider one of first notes she wrote after her mom death as an eulogy. The relationship between them  was a quite tight when you contemplate the words they were using on the notes but obviously they were not spending enough time with each other which make it harder to discuss merely small issues properly. <br />Maybe the message beyond this book is that we must spend enough  quality and quantity time  with our beloveds and never take our tiny graces for granted because we may lose them in a blink of an eye.<br /><br />I had high expectation about this book due to high rated reviews from many people but I was not pretty satisfied while reading, suffice to say that It was a bad choice.<br /> </span>

    <a title="YoSafBridg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/440929-yosafbridg"><img alt="YoSafBridg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1211664027p2/440929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22887890?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YoSafBridg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YoSafBridg" href="/user/show/440929-yosafbridg">YoSafBridg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/440929-yosafbridg?shelf=own-and-read">own-and-read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22887890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6131753199114928886">"This is Just to Say<br/>I have eaten<br/>the plums<br/>that were in<br/>the icebox<br/>and which<br/>you were probably<br/>saving<br/>for breakfast<br/>Forgive me<br/>they were delicious<br/>so sweet<br/>and so cold"<br/>~WILLIAM CARLOS WILLIAMS<br/>I remember when i first encountered this poem~ninth grade Honors English (my all time favorite teacher~most inspirational~props again Mr. Mathis...) I seem to remember one of those painful sessions of analyzation~searching for meaning, symbolism, wondering if there were any right or wrong answers (which brings back ni</span>
  <span id="freeText6131753199114928886" style="display:none">"This is Just to Say<br />I have eaten<br />the plums<br />that were in<br />the icebox<br />and which<br />you were probably<br />saving<br />for breakfast<br />Forgive me<br />they were delicious<br />so sweet<br />and so cold"<br />~WILLIAM CARLOS WILLIAMS<br />I remember when i first encountered this poem~ninth grade Honors English (my all time favorite teacher~most inspirational~props again Mr. Mathis...) I seem to remember one of those painful sessions of analyzation~searching for meaning, symbolism, wondering if there were any right or wrong answers (which brings back nightmares of yet another teacher~this time college and sixteenth century poetry~everything i said and wrote~was WRONG, WRONG, WRONG and somehow i could do better~it was the first time that i really understood what it felt like to be the "picked-upon-'dumb'-student"~absolutely hated it [this same teacher was also my English minor advisor and in advising sessions he was perfectly pleasant~nice even...) Anyway, couldn't this famous poem (and i do love the poem~perhaps just for its lovely simplicity) just be a note left on the kitchen table or the refrigerator door?<br />Alice Kuipers' first novel, life on the refrigerator door is just that~notes between a mother and daughter left on the refrigerator door (a somewhat refreshing form of communication in this day of cell phones, email, and im-ing). This is a wonderful book; its 220 pages can be easily read in less than a few hours, but the emotions will linger long after the last page is finished.<br />It is as touching (if not more so) for what is left unsaid as what is said. I have an advanced reader's edition which i picked up because it was there and it looked undaunting. Today while i was cataloging (ever the librarian, i) newly acquired books (unfortunately a few still accumulate though i have tried to curb certain impulses...) i picked it up, started reading and couldn't stop.<br />I never felt like Kuipers was constrained by her form and what went untold could be sensed through what was told. You know from the blurbs that all will not go well with these characters but it is still a most compelling read: short, sweet, and entirely moving... <br />I will leave you with one of Claire's notes to her mother:<br />"When I look at you<br />I see the woman I want to be<br />Strong and brave<br />Beautiful and free<br />Claire<br />P.S. I love you"<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6131753199114928886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_10790603" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10790603" />
    <a title="J-Lynn Van Pelt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/215947-j-lynn-van-pelt"><img alt="J-Lynn Van Pelt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1247498180p2/215947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10790603?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J-Lynn Van Pelt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J-Lynn Van Pelt" href="/user/show/215947-j-lynn-van-pelt">J-Lynn Van Pelt</a>

        rated it

A great example of how alternative formats can be just as strong as powerful as the traditional novel.<br/><br/>I like how the author didn't fill in the blanks, the reader is left to decide what conversations and fights take place between the daily notes.   <span id="freeText7477702144694444321" style="display:none">This book is incredibly moving especially when you think about the fact that it is written entirely in scribbled notes on the refrigerator door. A great example of how alternative formats can be just as strong as powerful as the traditional novel.<br /><br />I like how the author didn't fill in the blanks, the reader is left to decide what conversations and fights take place between the daily notes. In short notes, Kuipers captures the voice of a teenage girl and her mother struggling to fit cancer into their already busy lives. The final notes from the daughter are both heart-breaking and inspiring.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10383149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer119820466478168274">Such a quick read, think I had it finished in under an hour. I really didn't like most of this book. It seemed so wrong to me that this family of two couldn't take the time to communicate face-to-face. Although they do talk about a few meetings, most of the book centered around the fact that they didn't really know each other and were both so selfish they wouldn't stop anything in their own lives to spend time with each other. The mother knew little to nothing about the daughters school and soci</span>
  <span id="freeText119820466478168274" style="display:none">Such a quick read, think I had it finished in under an hour. I really didn't like most of this book. It seemed so wrong to me that this family of two couldn't take the time to communicate face-to-face. Although they do talk about a few meetings, most of the book centered around the fact that they didn't really know each other and were both so selfish they wouldn't stop anything in their own lives to spend time with each other. The mother knew little to nothing about the daughters school and social life, and the daughter seemed to retaliate by not getting to know anything about her mother's cancer when it was first found. I can't believe people really live like this. <br /><br />The end is what caught me though. So sad, so real. The end made it clear that they were both sorry they had lived their life that way and they learned what they needed to from each other. We miss all of the information they get from each other since they aren't done on paper, but we see that not only do they fix their communication problems, but they learn that they depended on even those notes that held them together.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10016141136719751517">This was a really quick read as the format of the book is conversation through post-it notes and eventually, a letter. This made the book an extremely quick read, but unfortunately I think that this didn't make the book as effective as it could be.   <span id="freeText10016141136719751517" style="display:none">This was a really quick read as the format of the book is conversation through post-it notes and eventually, a letter. This made the book an extremely quick read, but unfortunately I think that this didn't make the book as effective as it could be. Cancer is a quite shocking and a very emotive subject, but I just couldn't connect or feel much towards this book. It was all very quick and I although I thought that the post-it notes were a clever idea, I just can't believe that a mother and daughter would rely on this method of communication, especially at such a difficult time. I thought that it was all just a little too unrealistic and the conversation that the mother and daughter did have could've been more effective. Unfortunately, this just didn't work for me.</span>

<div id="review_2716805972" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2716805972" />
    <a title="Paty Pana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40790872-paty-pana"><img alt="Paty Pana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504176762p2/40790872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2716805972?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paty Pana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paty Pana" href="/user/show/40790872-paty-pana">Paty Pana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781509801879" href="/book/show/26127829-life-on-the-refrigerator-door">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40790872-paty-pana?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40790872-paty-pana?shelf=short-reads">short-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40790872-paty-pana?shelf=giveaway-wins">giveaway-wins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40790872-paty-pana?shelf=illness">illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2716805972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15999564818500733189"><b>I MAY HAVE FAILED AN EXAM BECAUSE OF THIS BOOK</b><br/>But don’t worry, this review will be a 5 star one!<br/><br/>I am still waiting for this exams results, but I just couldn’t resist this new book staring at me? And then it made it impossible to study after reading the last page? It was an absolutely bad decision to read this in the middle of the night instead of preparing for the next days important exams but… that’s priorities right? 0:)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Mom,<br/>I went to the store. See inside the fridge. I watered the plan</b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15999564818500733189" style="display:none"><b>I MAY HAVE FAILED AN EXAM BECAUSE OF THIS BOOK</b><br />But don’t worry, this review will be a 5 star one!<br /><br />I am still waiting for this exams results, but I just couldn’t resist this new book staring at me? And then it made it impossible to study after reading the last page? It was an absolutely bad decision to read this in the middle of the night instead of preparing for the next days important exams but… that’s priorities right? 0:)<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Mom,<br />I went to the store. See inside the fridge. I watered the plants. I cleaned out Peter’s cage. I tidied the sitting room. And the kitchen. And I did the washing up.<br />I’m going to bed.<br /><br />Your live-in servant,<br />Claire</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>A BIT ABOUT THE BOOK:</b> Have you ever read a book written solely in notes? No. not like Everything, Everything that had many of them. I mean just notes, no full pages- just notes attached to the refrigerator door! I found the idea very appealing and I knew I had to get this book. Then the plot came in and I got an extra reason to need it. Through the notes that are found each day on the refrigerator door, we get to know the relationship between Elizabeth and her daughter, Claire. They make their small family, just the two of them, but they never have enough time for each other. Elizabeth is a doctor and Claire a student that spends her free time with her friends or babysitting. And then… a different note is found on the refrigerator door… A note that lets Claire know her mom got an appointment with a doctor because she noticed something at her breast. And life changes.<br /><br /><b>I told you it wasn’t going to be a happy story. Oh, oops, I didn’t, and you just fell in my handcrafted lake of despair.</b><br /><br /><b>Likes: </b><br /><br /><b>♥ </b>I promise I have feelings but for some reason I love heart breaking books. They just depict the real world that isn’t always perfect. Someone may get sick. Someone may even die unexpectedly and we can do nothing to predict or prevent it at times. So the only thing we can do, is make our lives worthy. Memorable. I don’t know when saying I love you to our family or friends became something to feel but not something to be expressed. I thought of it a lot while reading this book.<br />♥<b>♥ </b>admirable. Telling a story that touches the reader’s heart within a book that doesn’t contain a full page-this takes some talent. And it’s not that the plot lacked in any part, everything you need to know is written in the exchanged notes. The good and the bad times, the fear and hope all live their mark on their refrigerator.<br /><b>♥ </b> I have never read a whole book in a day, and the fact that I even neglected my studies to finish this one in one sitting should mean something. It really made my heart be shattered in pieces and I wanted to wake up my mom and hug her. I was sobbing. If a book is so powerful, it may be actually able to change lives and bring us people together- What a blessing it would be!<br /><b>♥ </b>It also has something to teach to teenagers. Adolescence is the time when we start to feel we need to strengthen our bonds with peers, and this is acceptable and so natural. But in the process of seeking independence and freedom, teens can sometimes neglect their parents. Growing up should build the age gap and not enlarge it. When Claire spent all time with her friend and bf, I felt her mom was so alone… and I cried again.<br /><br /><b>THE COVER IS DAMN SILVER! </b><br /><br />♥♥♥If you want to try a one of a kind book, you can <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Life-on-Refrigerator-Door-Alice-Kuipers/9781509801879?ref=grid-view&amp;qid=1550277165061&amp;sr=1-1/?a_aid=onemorechap" rel="nofollow noopener">get “Life on the refrigerator door” HERE</a> ♥♥♥</span>
  <a data-text-id="15999564818500733189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1922010311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1922010311" />
    <a title="Mia B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59019726-mia-b"><img alt="Mia B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472305571p2/59019726.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1922010311?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mia B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mia B" href="/user/show/59019726-mia-b">Mia B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1922010311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5318813340211790581">Life on the Refrigerator Door by Alice Kuipers is a heartfelt story of a mother and daughter relationship. This novel is realistic fiction. The theme of this book is, “there’s always enough time.” Now, if you have read this book, you may wonder why I chose this theme. If you haven’t read it, it is about a girl, Claire, and her mother. Claire’s parents are getting a divorce, but Claire lives with her mom. Both girls are very, very busy. Claire obviously has to go to school, but she is also always</span>
  <span id="freeText5318813340211790581" style="display:none">Life on the Refrigerator Door by Alice Kuipers is a heartfelt story of a mother and daughter relationship. This novel is realistic fiction. The theme of this book is, “there’s always enough time.” Now, if you have read this book, you may wonder why I chose this theme. If you haven’t read it, it is about a girl, Claire, and her mother. Claire’s parents are getting a divorce, but Claire lives with her mom. Both girls are very, very busy. Claire obviously has to go to school, but she is also always studying, with friends, or hanging out with her boyfriend. Claire’s mom also has a lot on her plate being a full time nurse. Claire’s mom then finds out that she has breast cancer, which was a shock to them both. This then increases her mom’s busy schedule with many, many doctors appointments for treatment. The two girls rarely, if ever talk to each other. That is what makes this book such a quick read. Since the two girls don’t ever have time to talk, it is written in post-it notes between the mom and daugther. The lack of interaction between Claire and her mother, upsets them both. As if that is not enough, Claire also really struggles with the fact knowing her mom has cancer. I think the theme is “there’s always enough time” because Claire needed to find time to make to just say hi to her mom, even when it may have been impossible. Considering her mom’s conditions, she needed to figure out what she could do, to cherish the last moments with her mom. The author made you feel like you were there because it is relatable. My mom doesn’t have cancer, however, we have a strong bond, like Claire and her mom. Not all girls, but most have a strong bond with their mom, like me, which is why this book is relatable. I personally loved this author's writing style because of the post-it notes. I had never seen, or read, something like this. If the author had not done this, the book would have lost some of it’s “flair” almost. The mood of the book would definitely be different because the whole thing would just be dialogue, which would also be boring. I would definitely recommend this book to anyone. I think girls would enjoy it more, just because it is a mother daughter book. In conclusion, if you have the time, I would highly suggest reading this heart-wrenching story, that allows you to shed a few tears, because it is breathtaking. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5318813340211790581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3412328195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2700598732882001631">A pediatrician who is a single mother, her fifteen year old daughter, a cancer diagnosis and their life over an year. Just in notes on a refrigerator door. No context setting, no description of their home or surroundings, no soliloquies, no other conversation between them or with any other characters, just these notes. And the notes? Perfunctory, as between any other mother and her teenaged daughter. Yet, the depth of emotions it conveys!<br/><br/>Reading between the lines, literally that is what this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText2700598732882001631" style="display:none">A pediatrician who is a single mother, her fifteen year old daughter, a cancer diagnosis and their life over an year. Just in notes on a refrigerator door. No context setting, no description of their home or surroundings, no soliloquies, no other conversation between them or with any other characters, just these notes. And the notes? Perfunctory, as between any other mother and her teenaged daughter. Yet, the depth of emotions it conveys!<br /><br />Reading between the lines, literally that is what this book is. You form a clear picture of their friends, the father who is still a part of their lives, the diagnosis, the mother’s reactions as a woman, a mother and as a doctor, the daughter’s romance, her life in school, relationship with her father, the teenage tantrums, how she faces her mother’s illness, how both of them find acceptance and support in each other, yes all these in just notes on the refrigerator.<br /><br />All of a hundred and twenty one pages on an ebook, a delightful and heartwarming story told in a brilliant manner. Yes, just between the lines on a few refrigerator notes.<br /><br />Strongly recommended.<br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText13124588068802988419" style="display:none">A very quick read but emotional. <br /><br />I liked this book. It's a roller coasters of emotions between a mother and a daughter who leave notes on the fridge for each other because their schedule are so different and busy. Claire is a 15 year old teenager going to school, being with friends and dealing with a boyfriend, while her mother works at the hospital and has a busy sporadic work schedule. <br /><br />Once bad news hits you see the notes change between the mothers and daughter. <br /><br />As every mother and daughter they fight, the have fun together and they deal with issues together but some of the issues and questions written in the notes were really serious and I thought were questions that should have been discussed in person or at least in a phone call not in notes.<br /><br />I would have liked maybe dates on the notes just to know how sporadic the notes were. The sections in the book just tell you what time of year it is in chunks. January, March, June, and September.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book and it did make me feel emotion at the end of the book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13124588068802988419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4456807077492711900">I found <i>Life on the Refrigerator Door</i> in the super-discount bin at Barnes&Noble, thought it was an interesting concept and picked it up. <br/><br/>It wasn't a fantastic book and only took me about 40 minutes to read, but it certainly had a strong message.<br/><br/>This epistolary work is written in the form of notes between a mother and daughter left on the refrigerator as they just miss each other going through the motions of their busy lives. <br/><br/>When I first read the book, I felt both mother and daughter were selfis</span>
  <span id="freeText4456807077492711900" style="display:none">I found <i>Life on the Refrigerator Door</i> in the super-discount bin at Barnes&amp;Noble, thought it was an interesting concept and picked it up. <br /><br />It wasn't a fantastic book and only took me about 40 minutes to read, but it certainly had a strong message.<br /><br />This epistolary work is written in the form of notes between a mother and daughter left on the refrigerator as they just miss each other going through the motions of their busy lives. <br /><br />When I first read the book, I felt both mother and daughter were selfish and over-dramatic. However, the more I reflect on the novel, the more real the characters have become. Faced with a dire situation at home, they both have very believable reactions to the crisis. <br /><br />I am, however, still angry at the characters for not sitting down to talk about the problems they were facing. But I suppose that's the message - to not wait until it's too late to spend time with the ones you love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4456807077492711900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText46076507520032226" style="display:none">We went out to have lunch today at Nandos and before we went home, I popped into the bookstore. I was browsing when I saw this book. I walked away from it though because it looked like the stereotypical YA novel. But later on, I found myself drifting back to it. I picked it up, it had a pretty cover, and flipped to the first page. I quickly realised that the book was written in completely in notes and lists.<br /><br /> <b>So I started to read. And read. And read. And I finally finished the book.</b><br /><br />There were tears and I was trying to hide them desperately. This book broke my heart.<br /><br />When I was 14, I used to write emails to my dad. He worked late and I usually only saw him for about a half hour in the mornings when he dropped me in school so we would communicate a lot of the time through texts and emails and we worked through a lot of tough issues through these emails.I told him what I felt he needed to change about his life and he explained why he got angry at me over something. I also complained about my teachers and friends quite a bit.<br /><br />I was always better at writing and it helped me communicate with him in the most honest way that I could. But we always agreed to never ever to take the issue off the page. Meaning that after we had talked it out over email, we were never ever to say a word about it again in real life. It was a good system that stopped when I left secondary school. Now I make time to talk to my dad face to face.<br /><br />But reading this book brought that back and my goodness that ending where she kept writing to her mother killed me on the inside. This was such a random read but it impacted me a lot. Everyone should read it. Just take 30 minutes out of your life to read this beautiful little book. You won't regret it. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="46076507520032226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1507942103" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1507942103" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2262926-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420907415p2/2262926.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1507942103?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/2262926-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330456456" href="/book/show/1951116.Life_on_the_Refrigerator_Door">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1507942103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10844880195850252641"><i>Never judge a book by its cover.</i> You can say that again!<br/><br/>When I reached for <i>Life on the Refrigerator Door</i> at four in the morning I hoped for a light reading that would distract me from the stabbing pain in my stomach. Instead, I ended up being punched by a rather raw wave of emotion that I was not expecting at all.<br/><br/>Honestly, I find it hard to believe that people would communicate like this. I mean, at first it made sense. Even though plain - I thought this was going to be sort of a scrapbook thing</span>
  <span id="freeText10844880195850252641" style="display:none"><i>Never judge a book by its cover.</i> You can say that again!<br /><br />When I reached for <i>Life on the Refrigerator Door</i> at four in the morning I hoped for a light reading that would distract me from the stabbing pain in my stomach. Instead, I ended up being punched by a rather raw wave of emotion that I was not expecting at all.<br /><br />Honestly, I find it hard to believe that people would communicate like this. I mean, at first it made sense. Even though plain - I thought this was going to be sort of a scrapbook thing -, I expected it to lead us to a world similar to the one of <i>Mean Girls</i> and <i>Ten Things I Hate About You</i>. The boyfriend conversations, the <i>your-job-is-more-important-than-me</i> discussions, the <i>I-am-going-to-Dad's</i> rebellion... I honestly thought that was where we were headed. Now what came next...<br /><br /><i>That escalated rather quickly.</i><br /><br />I don't believe such topic would ever be discussed through refrigerator notes. And yet, if one chooses to ignore that <i>tiny</i> detail... There's so much <i>feeling</i>. It amazes me how Alice Kuipers was able to convey so much emotion through so little words. It's absolutely <i>heartbreaking</i>. <br /><br /><i>Life on the Refrigerator Door</i> asks for an extremely empathic reader, one that will read and feel through the lines. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I believe what brought me to tears was the fact that not even a week ago I lost someone to the <i>pink</i>. She left a note on the fridge, though. A last one to remind us that all the others written before, whether in paper, smiles or tears, will always live. As will she. In us. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="10844880195850252641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/220833473?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/5534520-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer220833473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2927129175429348960">I can't believe I wasted 20 minutes of my life on a self-centered mother-daughter duo who opt to discuss the weighty issue of breast cancer on the refrigerator door. Yup, you read that right. Nowhere in the books description did it mention breast cancer or I would never have downloaded it from my library. I lost my mother to breast cancer when I was only a couple years younger than the daughter in this book, so I found it even more insulting. And then I realized this drivel is actually targeted </span>
  <span id="freeText2927129175429348960" style="display:none">I can't believe I wasted 20 minutes of my life on a self-centered mother-daughter duo who opt to discuss the weighty issue of breast cancer on the refrigerator door. Yup, you read that right. Nowhere in the books description did it mention breast cancer or I would never have downloaded it from my library. I lost my mother to breast cancer when I was only a couple years younger than the daughter in this book, so I found it even more insulting. And then I realized this drivel is actually targeted at teens? I loved the idea of a novel that is based on Post-It notes with the reader imagining the untold story. But this is NOT that novel. This is a marketing ploy tied up with a pink ribbon. The only good thing I can say about this tripe is that it wound up being only 40 pages on my Nook. <br /><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HNuaMRXPiEyRtsEMjNjsBFwTV/pcaMvAFvd6x2p7VB7xYvTiVmG8/ax2efzWa70BceGp8JkRgipWNXMOsm9TJw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WleU2LqZqdYhtZDIYy7mZypZUhYjQD7C59FXiScBFh637voL+TedZxx1KDg5nbdiB6usHOY5dyinE15A/xURJw==')})
  }

القاتل، الذي يبدو فاهماً للأمر كله وعارفاً بمصير القرية. ما يلفت في شخصية علي صالح هو أنه الوحيد الذي أعرب عن رغبته في الرحيل، عندما اعترف بجريمة القتل وأصر عليها، بل أصر على التمسك بالطبعة المنطقية العودة&quot;، كما يصور المؤلف إسلام أهل القرية الذي لا صلة له بالتطرف أو الجماعات المتشددة ، وهي قرية متصالحة مع نفسها وتاريخها، ويحتقر فيها سفك الدماء ويجرم أكثر من جرائم الشرف ..\n\nالكاتب الصحفي We live in Saskatoon, Saskatchewan, which took a while for me to learn how to spell. I have four children, a girl and three boys.<br><br>My first novel, Life on the Refrigerator Door, was published in 29 countries, won several awards and was named as a New York Times book for the Teen Age. My second is called Lost For Words in the US, and The Worst Thing She Ever Did everywhere else. It won the Arthur Ellis Award, was shortlisted for the White Pine and Willow Awards, and was published in eight territories. 40 Things I Want To Tell You is my YA book published in 2012. The Death of Us, a CLA honour book, in 2014. My newest YA novel is Me (and) Me.<br><br>Violet and Victor Write the Best-Ever Bookworm Book is my first picture book. It was published with Little, Brown Books For Young Readers in December 2014, and the sequel Violet and Victor Write The Most Fabulous Fairy Tale is available now.<br><br>Find me at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.alicekuipers.com">www.alicekuipers.com</a></span>
